## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of second-order oscillator models. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators typically combine restoring forces from a nonlinear potential (functions of x) with damping/forcing terms (functions of v and t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Conservative linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring force; no damping/forcing)
- Linearly damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Shifted equilibrium (biased spring): dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) - c2 * v (offset equilibrium position)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring + damping)
- Quintic stiffness oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (stronger amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear pendulum (sine restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (large-angle pendulum dynamics with damping)
- Piecewise/impact-like stiffness via absolute value: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x - c2 * v (effective stiffness increases with |x|)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent dissipation)
- Quadratic drag with direction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * Abs(v) * v (aerodynamic-type damping)
- van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (self-excited via v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (limit-cycle oscillator with velocity nonlinearity)
- Externally driven oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic forcing in time)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type structure)
- General Liénard form: dv_dt = -f(x) * v - g(x) with f(x)=c0 + c1 * x**2, g(x)=c2 * x + c3 * x**3 (broad class covering many nonlinear oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring-force dominance → dv_dt primarily a function of x (often odd in x), indicating acceleration derives from a potential U(x) with dv_dt = -dU/dx.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening/softening) → include odd higher powers of x (x**3, x**5) or sin(x); these change effective stiffness with amplitude.
- Viscous dissipation → add a term -c * v; this causes energy to monotonically decrease and trajectories to spiral toward equilibrium in phase space.
- Nonlinear dissipation (drag) → include -c * v**3 or -c * Abs(v) * v; damping grows rapidly with speed and suppresses large-velocity motion.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior → damping coefficient depends on state (e.g., (c0 - x**2) * v or v - v**3), giving negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic driving → additive term in t such as c * cos(c * t) or c * sin(c * t), producing forced resonance and steady-state oscillations.
- Parametric resonance → time-varying stiffness multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x), which can amplify oscillations even without additive forcing.
- Non-smooth stiffness/contact effects → Abs(x) * x (or similar) creates different effective stiffness for large displacements, mimicking piecewise springs or geometric stiffening.
- Bias/offset equilibrium → use (x - c) inside restoring terms; indicates equilibrium position is not at x = 0 due to preload, gravity projection, or asymmetric constraints.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO9)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
f(x,t,v)=0.3064552763\sin t\;-\;0.4243105872\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.9272891093\,x\big(0.06821634757|v|^{1/3}+1\big)\;-\;1.9272891093\,x.
\]
Rewrite key structure:
- Sinusoid: \(A\sin t\) with **no exponential envelope**.
- Damping-like polynomial term: \(-0.4243\,v + 0.4243\,v x^2\) (i.e., linear in \(v\) plus \(v x^2\)).
- Restoring terms in \(x\): a linear term \(-1.9273x\) and an additional linear term \(-1.9273x\) (so total \(-3.8546x\)).
- Crucially: a non-polynomial term \(-1.9273\cdot 0.0682163\; x\,|v|^{1/3}\), i.e. **\(x\cdot |v|^{1/3}\)**. This absolute-value fractional-power dependence on \(v\) must be present to match globally (since \(v\) can be negative).

So any candidate must be able to represent simultaneously:
1) \( \sin t\) (phase shift allowed),
2) \(v\) and \(v x^2\),
3) \(x\),
4) **\(x|v|^{1/3}\)** (or an algebraically identical form).

Now check candidates.

1. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2\sin(c3 t+c4)+ c5 v(c6+x)^2\)  
Expanding last term gives \(v(x^2+2c6 x+c6^2)\): produces \(v\), \(vx\), \(vx^2\). Can match the polynomial-in-\(v\) pieces and \(\sin t\) and \(x\). But **cannot produce \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**. ⇒ No.

2. Adds \(c8 x\cos(c9 t)\). Still only polynomial in \(v\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Also introduces time-modulated \(x\) unless set to 0. ⇒ No.

3. Adds \(c7 x\sin(c8 t+c9)\). Same issue: no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

4. Adds \(c7 e^{c8 t}\log(c9|x|+1)\). Still no \(x|v|^{1/3}\); also wrong functional form in \(x\) unless zeroed. ⇒ No.

5. Polynomial terms in \(v\), \(vx^2\), plus \(t x\), \(x^3\), and an exponentially-modulated sinusoid. Can set unwanted terms to 0, but still **no \(x|v|^{1/3}\)**. Also sinusoid is \(e^{c6 t}\sin(\cdot)\); to match plain \(\sin t\) must set \(c6=0\), doable, but missing \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

6. Has \(v\), \(v x^2\), \(v^3\), plus \(e^{c7\cos x}\) term. No \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

7. Similar to 5 with constant term; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

8. Similar; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

9. Similar; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

10. Has \(t x\) and constant; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

11. Has \(v\) and \(v x^2\) and extra \(v\) again; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

12. No \(v\) at all except none; cannot match \(v\) terms. ⇒ No.

13. Has \(v\) and \(v x^2\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

14. Linear in \(x\), \(v\), \(v x^2\), plus exponential-sinusoid; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

15. Same; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

16. Has \(v x^2\) but lacks plain \(v\) unless via other terms (none). Also no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

17. Has \(v\) and \(v x^2\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

18. Has constant and \(v x^2\) but no plain \(v\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

19. Includes \(v^3\) and \(v(c8+t)^{c9}\) (time-dependent factor), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Also introduces \(t\)-dependent scaling of \(v\). Can zero those, but then still missing \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

20. Has \(v\sin(c8 x+c9)\) (nonlinear in \(x\) but still linear in \(v\)); cannot equal \(x|v|^{1/3}\) for all \(x,v\). ⇒ No.

21. Has \(v(c6+x)^3\) and \(x(c8+v)^{c9}\). The second term could create fractional powers of \(v\) if \(c9=1/3\), giving \(x(c8+v)^{1/3}\), but GT needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\) with absolute value and no shift. If set \(c8=0\), get \(x v^{1/3}\), which is **not real-valued for negative \(v\)** (and not equal to \(|v|^{1/3}\) anyway). If choose \(c8\neq 0\), it’s \((v+\text{const})^{1/3}\), not \(|v|^{1/3}\). No absolute value available. ⇒ No.

22. Has \(v(c6+x)^3\) and \(v(c8+x)^{c9}\): still only powers of \(x\) multiplying \(v\), not \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

23. Has \(x\), \(v\), \(t x\), exp-sinusoid, and a cosine in time. No \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

24. Has \(v x^{c9}\) (power on \(x\), not on \(|v|\)); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

25. No \(v\) dependence except none; cannot match \(v\) terms. ⇒ No.

26. Has \(x\log(c8|c9 v|+1)\). This uses \(|v|\) but inside a log, not \(|v|^{1/3}\). No way to choose constants to make \(\log(a|v|+1)\equiv k|v|^{1/3}\) for all \(v\). ⇒ No.

27. Has \(x(c8+v)^{c9}\) again; same issue as #21: no Abs, and shift breaks it; also real-valued issues for negative \(v\) if fractional exponent. ⇒ No.

28. Has \(v(c6+x)^3\) and \(x\sin(\cdot)\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

29. Has \(v\sin(\cdot)\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

30. Has \(v(c9+x)^3\) and extra sine; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

31. Only \(v(c6+x)^3\) plus sinusoid and \(x\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

32. Has \(v|v|\) (i.e., \(|v|^2\) with sign of \(v\)), not \(|v|^{1/3}\), and polynomial \(x^3,x^5\). Cannot match \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

33. Has \(v x^3\) and rational-in-\(t\) terms; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

34. Similar to 19/23; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

35. Has \(v|v|\) and \(x|x|\); still no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

36. Has \(v|v|\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

37. Has cosine in time plus other terms; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

38. Has \(v(c8+x)^{c9}\) (power on \(x\)); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

39. Has \(v|v|\) again; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

40. Has \(v^3\) and \(x^2\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

41. Has \(v|v|\); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

42. Has \(v\) and \(v^3\) and exp(cos x); no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

43. Has \(\log(c8 e^{c9 x}+1)\); no \(v\) dependence except via other terms (none besides \(v^3\) in this candidate). Missing \(v\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

44. Has \(v x^3\) and rational-in-\(t\) terms; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

45. Has \(v x^3\) and rational-in-\(t\) terms; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

46. Has \(v x^3\) and rational-in-\(x\) terms; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

47. Has \(v\) and \(v x^3\) and constant; no \(v x^2\) and no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

48. Has \(v x^3\) only; cannot match \(v\) and \(v x^2\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\). ⇒ No.

49. Same as 48 plus constant; still no. ⇒ No.

50. Has \(v/(a v+b)\) and \(1/(a v+b)\) plus \(v x^3\). No \(x|v|^{1/3}\); also wrong \(v\)-dependence. ⇒ No.

Conclusion: every candidate lacks the essential non-polynomial coupling term \(x\,|v|^{1/3}\) (with Abs and fractional power) present in the GT, and none can generate it via parameter choice while remaining globally valid for negative \(v\).

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO9)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*Abs(v)**c3 + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.424310587218182*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.92728910930903*x*(0.0682163475684738*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.92728910930903*x + 0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-0.424310587218182*v + 0.424310587218182*v*x**2`
- `-1.92728910930903*x*0.0682163475684738*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 1.92728910930903*x`
- `-1.92728910930903*x`
- `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

Combining x terms: `-1.92728910930903*x - 1.92728910930903*x = -3.85457821861806*x`

So GT = `-3.85457821861806*x - 0.424310587218182*v + 0.424310587218182*v*x**2 - 0.131498932685498*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + 0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `v` (linear)
3. `v*x**2`
4. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` — this is the critical term
5. `sin(t)`

The key distinguishing term is `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`. This involves a cube root of the absolute value of v multiplied by x. Let me check each candidate for this term.

Most candidates lack `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`. Let me scan for candidates that could potentially produce this term:

- Candidates 1-18, 20-37, 39-50: None contain `Abs(v)**(1/3)` or equivalent. They use terms like `v*x**2`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, `exp(cos(x))`, `x**3`, `t*x`, etc. None can produce `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`.

- **Candidate 19**: `c7*v*(c8 + t)**c9` — involves t, not Abs(v)**(1/3)
- **Candidate 22**: `c7*v*(c8 + x)**c9` — this is `v*(x+const)**power`, not `x*Abs(v)**power`
- **Candidate 24**: `c8*v*x**c9` — this is v times x to a power, not x times |v| to a power
- **Candidate 27**: `c7*x*(c8 + v)**c9` — this is `x*(v+const)**power`. If c8=0, c9=1/3, this gives `x*v**(1/3)`, but v takes both signs, so `v**(1/3)` isn't the same as `Abs(v)**(1/3)`.
- **Candidate 38**: Same as 27: `c7*v*(c8 + x)**c9` — wrong variable arrangement

None of the candidates contain the term `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`. Since `Abs(v)**(1/3)` is not equivalent to any polynomial, exponential, trigonometric, or other standard function present in the candidates, and it cannot be generated from the available basis functions, none of the candidates can match the GT.
